Shen Bao Wireless Radio Weekly

Method for Calibrating Multi-Stage Tuned Radio Receivers 216

— Li Yuanqing

丨The Use of an Experimental Oscillator丨

Once the tuning circuits of each stage of a high-frequency radio receiver lose their balance, its sensitivity, selectivity, volume, and sound quality will immediately be significantly affected, as mentioned in the article "Oscillator Testing Device" in Issue 79 of this publication. This article will further detail the method for calibrating multi-stage tuning circuits, so that readers can gain a comprehensive understanding.

No matter how complex a radio you construct, the tuning circuit of each stage is nothing more than a coil and a variable capacitor. Usually, the coils within the tuning circuits are almost always fixed, so if we want to calibrate a circuit that has lost its balance, we must start with the variable capacitor.

The multi-gang variable capacitors used in older radios were not designed to be perfect. In addition to a small trimmer capacitor attached to each section (see diagram T in Figure 2), there are no other adjustment settings. Therefore, during calibration, true resonance (Exact Resonance) can only be achieved at a certain point, and nothing else can be done.

Newer radios adopt variable capacitors where both the start and end movable plates of each section are modified into fan-shaped segments (Fan-shaped Segments) (as shown in Figures 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5). This eliminates the aforementioned shortcomings!

Figure 1 shows the most common method for calibrating tuning circuits: First, rotate the multi-gang variable capacitor of the radio until the first fan-shaped segment is half-inserted into the stator plate (as shown by the dotted line in Figure 2). Next, connect the A and G posts of the experimental oscillator (the attached diagram in Issue 79; the positive terminal of the B battery is directly grounded, which is not very convenient to use; now it is modified as shown in the diagram) directly to the antenna and ground terminals of the radio using shielded wire (see description below). Then, rotate the capacitor C to resonate with the radio. At this time, the reading on the milliampere meter in the series-connected detection tube plate circuit (if a milliampere meter is not available, a sensitive voltmeter can be used instead) will immediately increase (the diagram shows plate detection; if it is grid detection, the meter reading will decrease). Then, use a screwdriver to push each section's capacitor's first small plate one by one (except for the first section C2), while slightly moving the rotating shaft, until the meter reading reaches its maximum (or minimum) value. At this point, the calibration procedure for the first frequency band (frequency approximately from 1500 K·C· to 1120 K·C·; there are slight differences depending on the manufacturer) within the tuning circuit is completed. The calibration methods for the remaining second frequency band (frequency approximately from 1120 K·C· to 840 K·C·) up to the fifth frequency band (frequency approximately from 600 K·C· to 550 K·C·) are similar, so they will not be elaborated upon here.

The calibration method for tuning circuits has been described above. Now, some points to note during calibration will be added below:

1. The radio's antenna must be disconnected beforehand to avoid interference from external radio waves (but the ground wire must be connected).

2. The radio must be placed on a very dry table, and avoid being close to metal objects to prevent capacitance effects.

3. To avoid the radio from sensing the radio waves emitted by the oscillator and to maintain frequency stability, the oscillator must be installed in a shielded box.

4. Similarly, shielded wire is used for the antenna. The ground wire is transmitted through the shielding material (see Figure 1).

5. The screwdriver used to push the small plates of each section's capacitor must be made of insulating material (see "Insulated Screwdriver" in this issue).

6. The volume control must be turned to its maximum setting.

Report on Ultra-Shortwave Communication Experiment 217

— Bing Yi

The scorching and bothersome summer has finally passed, and the refreshing early autumn brings much joy and pleasant emotions. Let's think about playing with ultra-shortwaves. With a moment's excitement, I tried this ultra-shortwave communication experiment.

The circuit I used is the Uitraudion type. The Uitraudion is worth recommending for ultra-shortwave oscillators among common and simple circuits. Furthermore, in order to reduce leakage loss, the plate voltage is connected to the end near the grid, with a choke coil RFC2 connected in between. In this way, the high-frequency voltage received by the grid is lower than that of the plate. The complete diagram is as follows:

The values of the other components in the diagram are as follows:

C1 = 50 ufd,

C2 = 14 ufd or homemade, C3 = 100 ufd

C4 = 250 ufd

R1 = 30 ohms R2 = 0-50000 ohms

V = RCA 30 MT = Microphone transformer

M = Single-button microphone Ph = 2000 ohms sensitive earphone S = Switch or homemade

Method for making L1L2—Use a sturdy small dry battery casing, and soak it in wax. Wind two turns of bell wire around the middle part, with a distance of 1/15 inch, to make L2. Then, wind two turns across L2 with a distance of about 1/4 inch to make L1. (See Figure 2.) It must be wound tightly. Looseness will inevitably lead to frequency instability. L2 can be rotated on C1 without needing to be wired separately.

RFC—Use two 1/18 inch diameter plastic rods or pen tubes, cut into one inch lengths. First, glue a 1/4 inch wide strip of paper to each end to create a raised object (see Figure 3). Wind 30 gauge wire onto it sequentially, with the distance between each turn equal to the diameter of 26 gauge wire: (wind with a 30 gauge wire and a 26 gauge wire together, and then remove the 26 gauge wire).

MT—It is best to use an existing microphone transformer. The author used a larger iron core low-frequency transformer. The secondary winding was removed, and 250 turns of 32 gauge wire were wound. The effectiveness is also quite good. As for the microphone switch, a plug-in terminal can be used instead. Unplug the terminal when not speaking. The microphone battery and A battery can use a ready-made 4 1/2 volt C battery. See Figure 1 for the wiring method.

All wiring should be firmly soldered with solder. The coil and tuning capacitor should be kept away from the RFC. The panel is best made of aluminum plate. The baseplate is made of plastic board.

The above components must be prepared in duplicate to make two ultra-shortwave radios.

When the author first calibrated, the B battery used 45V. It did not oscillate. Later, when the voltage was increased to 90V, oscillation only occurred in the shortwave section. Later, the capacity of C2 was reduced, and when 67.5V was used for the B battery, the oscillation became stable. Therefore, when encountering the difficulty of not oscillating during initial calibration, the wiring of C1 and C2 can be temporarily disconnected. The minimum capacity of C2 should be chosen to be sufficiently small. Homemade can be made with two bent copper pieces standing opposite each other. Nail them to a plastic board. They can be moved closer or further to increase or decrease the capacitance. Once calibrated, there is no need to move them again, just control R2. C4 is used to prevent C2 from short-circuiting.

For this experiment, two 1.5 zhang long leather wires were used as antennas, erected upright in the courtyard. They were connected to either end of L1. During the initial calibration, the distance was extremely close. The range of received signals was extremely narrow. Because a fine-tuning dial was not used, adjustment felt quite difficult. The strength of the signals heard in the earphones was also not very strong. Later, the distance was gradually increased. The sharp hissing sound of the received signals was still the loudest at a distance of one or two dozen zhang. This is probably because the range is too narrow, and the human ear cannot distinguish it for a moment. The furthest distance was completed at the homes of Mr. Yisun and myself from this newspaper. The straight-line distance between us is about 1/3 of a li. The music and conversation that were broadcast were received very clearly. The gentle Merry Widow was heard very softly in the eardrums. There was no noise. There was no attenuation. What a good range!

Because the autumn school semester has arrived, we have stopped our experiment. Although these two machines feel simple and unsatisfactory in terms of production, I dare to introduce them to comrades who want to try playing with them for the reason that they are "guaranteed not to fail". It would be even better if they could be improved to greatly increase their effectiveness.

Simple Method for Repairing Broken Transformer Wires 218

— Yongyan

After a transformer or choke coil wire breaks, it must be disassembled and rewound, or its two wire ends must be connected to a 220-volt AC power line, using the electric welding effect to automatically reconnect the broken point. However, the former procedure is troublesome and daunting. The latter is very dangerous if a short circuit occurs; neither is a good method. Here is a safer method that can solve this problem. The method is as follows:

First, find a "spark coil" (Spsrk coil. This item is often available in ordinary physics laboratories). Connect its secondary winding to the two ends of the broken wire coil; connect the primary winding to a 6-volt storage battery, and connect a momentary switch in between to control the opening and closing of the current in the primary coil. Once the device is ready, press the momentary switch to open and close the current in the primary coil of the spark coil from time to time. After several times, the broken point of the broken wire coil can be soldered together. If it still fails to solder together after several power-ons, you can add one or two more 6-volt storage batteries to make it 12 or 18 volts to solder it together. However, sometimes this method will not work because the gap at the break is too large, and it must be disassembled and rewound.

When this method is used, only a momentary current flows through the coil being repaired, so it is not very dangerous. Moreover, the hope of soldering together is greater than using 220 volts, so it is introduced.

High-Performance Crystal Radio 219

— Cao Runsheng

Apart from reading, sleeping, and eating, I am almost always immersed in radio. Sometimes when I'm happy, I tinker with vacuum tube radios and try out audio. When I get tired of that, I go and play with crystal radios. The interest in playing with crystal radios is not as strong as that of vacuum tube radios. The reason is nothing more than that crystal radios have poor selectivity or insufficient volume. If the selectivity is good, the volume is not good, and if the volume is good, the selectivity becomes a mess.

Recently, I discovered a circuit with excellent performance. Not only is the selectivity extremely good, but the volume is also excellent, almost comparable to a single-tube radio. Now, I will record its circuit and the components used for comrades to study:

L1: 8 turns of 26 gauge enameled wire.

L2: 60 turns of the same gauge wire, with a tap at the 40th turn to connect to the crystal.

L3: 30 turns of the same gauge wire.

All three coils are wound on a spiderweb three-circuit coil frame.

C1, C2, C3: Three 0.00035 MFD variable capacitors.

C4: 0.002 MFD fixed capacitor.

Miscellaneous Talks 220

— Yongnian

(1) Radio Romance In Leicester, England, an amateur radio enthusiast named Wright is now crossing the Atlantic to marry an American girl he has never met. The matter is very strange, because Mr. Wright first obtained the echo of an American young radio enthusiast when he sent out a call from his self-built amateur shortwave radio station; therefore, they became friends through the medium of radio waves, and through this friend, he got to know Miss Fox in the United States through matchmaking. After several letters, they agreed, and Mr. Wright decided to set off for Michigan to marry Miss Fox. It is said that they plan to hold a wedding in the United States, and five days later, they will return to England with his newlywed wife. (Reuters dispatch)

(2) Wavelengths in Use The longest wavelength actually used in radio communications today is 20,000 meters. There are longer ones, but they have not been seen in use. The shortest is 1.5 meters. Shorter ones are still in scientists' laboratories.

(3) Vacuum Tube Production Until April 1934, vacuum tube manufacturers in the United States had manufactured a total of 130 types of radio vacuum tubes (only about half of which can be seen in Shanghai). The production volume of each type is thousands per minute, but for those made by Chinese people themselves, not a single one has been heard of in recent years.

A Battery with High Voltage 221

— Shudian

Since the prevalence of AC radios, the status of batteries in radio has certainly plummeted, but in small towns and villages, they are still unanimously supported by listeners.

There are four conditions that must be met when choosing a battery: (1) high voltage (2) durable voltage (3) long battery life (4) low cost. The dry batteries and storage batteries currently in use cannot meet the above conditions. Dry batteries are too expensive and have a short lifespan. Storage batteries are expensive to begin with, and the charging procedure is also very troublesome. A little carelessness during use will "sentence them to death." The author saw a type of battery in a Japanese "Intermediate Physics" book that meets the four conditions mentioned above and may be introduced to readers:

The battery being introduced now is simply a modified bichromate battery. This battery looks the same as a nitric acid battery from the outside, that is, an unglazed ceramic cylinder (i.e., unglazed cylinder) is placed in a large glass bottle. The cylinder is filled with a saturated potassium dichromate solution, and about 1/4 of sulfuric acid is added. A carbon rod is inserted into the cylinder. The bottle (i.e., outside the cylinder) is filled with a saturated potassium nitrate solution, and then a zinc cylinder is placed in. This step is completed.

This battery has a voltage of 2 Volts. According to the author's experiment, it can be used for three months. When the voltage drops, some sulfuric acid can be added to restore it.

1. Dry Battery Revival Method.

When a dry battery runs out of power, you can use the following method to revive it. If the zinc and skin on the outside are not damaged and are in good condition, you can punch a few holes around the zinc skin and inject some saturated ammonium chloride solution into the holes to restore the power. However, the maximum power can only reach 2/3 of the original. If the zinc skin is corroded, you can put the dry battery in a bottle filled with concentrated ammonium chloride solution. Its power can be restored to half of its original power. (These are all the author's attempts)

2. Protecting Hard Rubber Method

Hard rubber is easily decomposed when exposed to sunlight. Sulfur will precipitate on the surface in a thin layer and is easily broken. To avoid this drawback, shellac (Note) can be applied to the rubber. It is not afraid of the sun and is very beautiful: (Note) Shellac can be purchased at the Commercial Press Printing Office Library Department on Niuzhuang Road in this city, about two yuan per pound.

Radio Broadcasting in Japan (1) 222

— Cai Guanghua, sent from Tokyo

Like other countries in the world, the development of radio broadcasting in Japan in recent years has been very miraculous. In 1925, there were only three radio stations in Japan (Tokyo, Osaka, and Nagoya), and they were all privately operated. This was the budding era of radio broadcasting in Japan. In 1926, the Ministry of Communications, based on the British Broadcasting Act, adopted an absolute government intervention policy to assist in the establishment of the Broadcasting Corporation of Japan to manage the national and radio stations. The above-mentioned three private radio stations were also registered with the Association at the same time and were under the jurisdiction of the Association.

As for the so-called Japan Broadcasting Association, it nominally flaunts itself as a "corporate juridical person"丨a type of social organization subject to legal sanctions丨but in reality, most of the capital belongs to the government. The South Manchuria Railway Company, Japan Mail Steamship Company, etc. are all the same organizations, which are also a kind of far-sighted strategy of the Japanese government, because in this way, in the event that Japan starts a war with any country and is defeated, these many businesses can rely on the international law pretext that "victorious countries shall not seize the private businesses of defeated countries" and be protected, or at least, there can be some confusion without losing everything.

The Association's general headquarters is located in Tokyo. Its actual duty is to manage all national radio stations and engage in research on various radio businesses according to the wishes of the Ministry of Communications. Therefore, its rights are limited, and of course there will be no excessive actions. Its regular expenses are very sufficient, so it is responsible for the development of the radio business throughout Japan. (To be continued)

Free Talk

A Discussion on "The Climax in Literary Works" 223

— Laoyi

After reading Mr. Huang Huaibai's article "The Climax in Literary Works" published in the Free Talk on October 2, the general discussion is: the climax of a literary work is like the peak of a mountain, and the crest of a wave. Those who look at mountains must look at the highest peak, those who watch the tide must reach the rising crest; and those who appreciate literary works must look forward to the arrival of its "climax". This is an inevitable principle. Otherwise, if the climax is not found and the center of gravity is lost, the reader feels uninterested and the work does not become a work.

The passages that Mr. Huang cited, Daiyu burning manuscripts in "Dream of the Red Chamber", the necklace of "Necklace" which turns out to be a fake diamond, and Bazarov's death in "Fathers and Sons" are all the "climaxes" in their entire book, there are many points in the full text, it seems that his logical connection is like this. We try to think about it a little, and we feel that there is still a place for Mr. Huang to discuss.

The so-called "climax", first of all, we have such a question, in literary works, does it refer to the center of gravity of thought? Or does it refer to the ending of the story? (These are two things, not to be confused) According to his citations, it seems to refer to the ending of the story, not the center of gravity of thought. We know that the center of gravity of the thought of "Dream of the Red Chamber" lies in exposing the crimes of aristocratic families, and Daiyu burning manuscripts is its ending. The center of gravity of the thought of "Necklace" lies in warning those who are vain, and the confession of a fake diamond necklace is its ending. The center of gravity of "Fathers and Sons" lies entirely in explaining the contradiction between the thoughts of two different eras, and Bazarov's death is its ending. The facts are obvious and cannot be concealed. If so, in all literary works, no matter what the content of the thought is, there must be a statement of the story among the various contents; and the statement of the story must have an inevitable ending, about this, it seems that there is no need to say it. However, let's think a step further: the meaning of "climax" in literary works seems not only to be the ending of the story; but to make the ending of a story more exciting, and even to make it as exciting as possible 丨if that's the case, we should have another argument.

No one denies that people who truly appreciate literary works do not necessarily focus on the story; especially, they do not necessarily focus on whether the ending of the story is exciting. As long as the author's thoughts are correct, the emotions are full, and the text and other aspects of the technology are successful, then in the reader's mind. In any case, they are always chasing down word by word in a tense mood. What is the stimulation of the ending? What is the image of the "climax"? He has no time to think about it. For example: when we read Tolstoy's "War and Peace", we only feel its magnificence, vastness, and all the boundlessness at all times, everything seems to be tangible and intangible, unconsciously leading the reader's mind into a kind of vast ocean, only seeing the boundless sky, the boundless water, the boundless mist, the boundless waves, and not knowing where they have gone themselves? At that time, can you still think about what its ending will be? What about the "climax"? Moreover, the whole ending of "War and Peace" ends so ordinary, so little is stimulating, and it is not easy to find the "climax". But can "War and Peace" be said to be not great? The situation of "Water Margin" is also like this, the middle part is moving, and the ending is uninteresting, and it is even more inconvenient to find the so-called "climax" of the whole book. So, can the book "Water Margin" be considered a valuable work?

Taking a step back, even if a literary work must have its so-called "climax". Then, according to what Mr. Huang cited, we feel that in addition to the ending of the "Necklace" story, which cannot but be completed with the confession of a fake diamond necklace to form the so-called "climax" of the entire book; such as Bazarov's death in "Fathers and Sons", and Daiyu burning manuscripts in "Dream of the Red Chamber", at best, it only added another emotional stimulus in the reader's mind! After all, it has nothing to do with the value of the entire book. Moreover, the burning of manuscripts comes from Gao E's sequel, and Cao Xueqin's 80 chapters of "Dream of the Red Chamber" do not see it; but can Cao Xueqin's "Dream of the Red Chamber" be established, and can it have value?

Therefore, we can know that because of the exciting endings of the books "Necklace", "Fathers and Sons", and "Dream of the Red Chamber", Mr. Huang's so-called "climax" was aroused, and he even advocated that a literary work cannot succeed without its "climax". I think that a literary work can have a "climax" (if it can be called a climax), or it can have no "climax". The former is like "Necklace", and the latter is like "War and Peace" and "Water Margin", etc. Therefore, the establishment of a literary work is entirely due to the author's personality and skills to distinguish its multifaceted success. The theory of "climax" seems to be close to subjective in nature, and cannot summarize the meaning of the entire literary work.

Witch Gorge 224

— Duan Weitei

Arrived at the Jialing dock.

He was mysteriously puffing on a cigarette, the smoke clouding his face, which was as white as lightning.

Looking at that face, I felt a surge of anger.

However, the whistle of the American ship "Qichun" docked on the opposite bank had already sounded.

I had no choice but to restrain myself and jump onto a rowing boat with him.

Entered the third-class cabin.

As usual, he was smoking, his left leg crossed over his right, putting on an air of being experienced and worldly.

I could only stare at this person, a companion I'd shared for half a month, an indescribable partner.

The river water howled and cried.

And so, we endured for two days – eating, smoking, sleeping, smoking, shitting, smoking – my mood completely ruined by this person's way of life.

However, the ship had reached the Witch Gorge, where the wind roared, the waves surged, and the apes shrieked.

At that time, the pale yellow crescent moon was shining on the mountainside, which was surrounded by clouds. We jumped off the ship and sat in a rowing boat, gently, gently, approaching the pier of Kui Prefecture City, a dock made of piled-up rocks.

I stepped on my shadow, and he also stepped on his shadow. Together, we draped ourselves in the silver羽衣 of moonlight and stepped into this city, which had been carefully glanced over with cold, sharp eyes by many dead heroes, such as Zhuge Liang, Li Xiong, and Wang Jian.

I sat; he also sat. I sighed deeply; he also let out a long whistle. By the dim lamplight, filled with a sense of nostalgia for the past and sorrow for the present, I asked the locals about the local conditions. He held the cigarette butt tightly against the lamp and also said something out of place, "It's a pity, this place is too quiet."

I felt that this journey had become completely theatrical.

I wanted to express some complaints to this person, but I lacked sufficient reason. I could only hesitate, bury my head, and return to the ship cabin with a feeling of utter defeat.

Just as I was about to turn around and close the door of the third-class cabin, a slender finger, with earthworm-like blue veins, clutching the half-smoked cigarette butt, a hand that I was tired of seeing, had already stiffly reached into that glass door.

I could only force a smile.

The smoke, the gleaming, lightning-like face, the elegant crossed legs, continued to irritate me without violating any rules.

"Friend! Have you read something like this – my travel companion?"

I asked sarcastically.

"Hmm!" He was surprised, yet still leisurely blowing skillful smoke rings.

I knew that there was nothing more to be done in this situation.

When we arrived at Yichang, I decided to switch to the British ship "Shashi," a large Yangtze River steamer, heading towards Wuchang.

Stepping into berth number five in the second-class cabin of this ship, I took two steps back, cold sweat dripping from my forehead, I discovered an astonishing miracle.

The truth of the matter was this.

He was already lying comfortably in the first berth, immersed in a sweet dream, a smile of contentment playing on his lips, also pillowing a newly bought pack of "Beautiful" brand cigarettes!

I was speechless.

In my heart, I was only shouting strangely:

"Drug dealer? Magician? Detective? ......"

I could only frankly blame fate, blame this unlucky stretch of water, what other way was there to avoid it!

I thought that this extraordinary story within the ordinary is something that every old traveler has inadvertently encountered.

A British Man's Quick Sketch of the World's Three Great Cities 225

— Te

New York! A noisy, optimistic, and melancholic city where people speak casually. It has cool cinemas, soaring skyscrapers, extremely extravagant millionaires, and paupers who lack food and clothing. It is a magnet for people from all countries who want to find opportunities to get rich.

London! Immersed in traditional customs. There, you can often see the King and Queen pass by the gates of Buckingham Palace in a carriage. In nightclubs or restaurants, you might suddenly find yourself sitting next to the Prince of Wales. On Fleet Street, you will bump into the robust and extraordinary spirit of Dr. Johnson. London is the world's clearinghouse.

Paris! Is cheerful, fun, and irresponsible. It is a playground for wealthy Americans. It is a gathering place for American girls, garment workers, perfume makers, cheap wine, good restaurants, and glib men and women. If you give the driver too little tip there, he will throw it in your face. (After you leave, he will pick it up from the roadside ditch.) Paris, its happy, thick crust, just covers up all the suffering inside.

If someone asks you: "Where are you going to live soon? London, Paris, New York, which place would you choose?"

New York can be considered the most comfortable city to live in. Its perfect heating and cooling equipment is unmatched anywhere else. People living in London feel very uncomfortable when they encounter extremely hot or cold weather, because there is no air conditioning when it's hot and no heating when it's cold in homes, restaurants, cinemas, and trains." Parisians do not like fresh cold air, so most of the indoor areas have sophisticated heating equipment, but the equipment for heat protection is completely lacking. In the summer, the sultry heat in homes and hotels is very uncomfortable.

In New York, the kitchens of ordinary people are almost all equipped with automatic dishwashers, but in London and Paris, only wealthy families can enjoy this convenience. Because New York has a very complete transportation system, fresh fruits and vegetables are often available year-round. In London and Paris, berries and peas are impossible to buy in winter.

Parisian bathrooms would make New York housewives cry. Once, I was staying with some people from the bourgeoisie, and I asked them, "Where is the bathroom? I want to take a bath." They all looked at me in surprise, and ultimately because I was British, they shrugged, forgave me, led me to a small, dark room, and left. I looked around, and there was only a small tin basin inside, which was not clean inside or out. I hesitated for a while and decided to give up the dubious pleasure of a bath, and then I came out.

Besides being comfortable to live in, what other advantages does New York have?

New York's telephone service is the most responsive in the world. Once, when I was living in Paris, it took me 20 minutes to connect a phone call to a friend on the next street. I once made a phone call from New York to London, and it was connected in 10 minutes.

New York women's clothing is both cheaper and more beautiful than in Paris and London, but men's clothing is more expensive than anywhere else in the world.

New York's dental advancements far surpass those of London. European dentists only have to say that they studied in the United States, and they can charge high surgical fees. This is their only way to make money. Because Americans are generous and charitable, New York's hospitals are well-equipped, which cannot be matched elsewhere. The hospital run by Americans in Paris never has an empty bed.

London is a good place to live. A famous painter said to me, "New York is a good place to work and make money, but when it comes to living, I prefer London. Look: its street names, like Royal Street and Lincoln's Inn, are very suitable for family life. As for New York's street names, like East 32nd Street and West 62nd Street, they are unbearably vulgar and make people feel disgusted." Many Americans only go to London for a short trip, but there are also many who live there for comfort.

Londoners are very careful in choosing friends, but once they become friends, they never forget them in their lifetime. Years ago, when I was in New York, many people became friends with me at first sight and were willing to form eternal friendships with me, vowing oaths that were extremely moving. Recently, when I went to New York again, only three people still remembered me. Some had also left New York and lived elsewhere. Many of the others acted as if they didn't know me when we met. Sometimes I would call them, and the reply was always, "Graham? I'm sorry, I don't recognize you!"

Londoners are calm and have few emotions (except before the King and Queen appear before the public or when a famous actress takes the stage). They are not like New Yorkers or Parisians, who can be as hot as fire one moment and as cold as ice the next.

The lives of Parisians are completely different from the lives of English and American travelers. They reluctantly greet foreigners who come to Paris for pleasure with a smile, but as long as foreigners are willing to spend money, they can go wherever they want.

Parisians are very hardworking, they get up early and go to bed late. The cooking in the restaurants is very good and very clean. Every night, gentlemen mostly take their wives to their favorite restaurants, only eat two dishes, and spend four hours talking. Parisians love music very much, and many cafes hire two or three violinists and a pianist.

Paris is more beautiful than London and New York. Places like the tricolor Champs-Élysées, the Place Vendôme, and the Bois de Boulogne are all unparalleled. The architecture in Paris is very orderly, and the rent is cheaper than in London and New York.

Parisians hate foreigners even more than the British. It is rare to find an Englishman or an American among their friends. Their personalities are wild and unrestrained, and they like to joke with people (especially mischievous ones), taking jokes as everyday fare. They believe that life is a kind of teasing created by God, and people should laugh and be happy; crying is the behavior of fools.

Each of these three great cities has its own advantages, and it is very difficult to choose one.

A very smart person once said, "Living in each place for one-third of the year, that's the only way to fully appreciate their advantages."

Little Comprador (2) 226

— Written by Langston Hughes, translated by Folang

This hotel has no attached dining room, only five tea servers besides Cindy. The head of these tea servers, old Willis, is often seated near the tables. There are two maids who prepare the food in the kitchen, they work in the mornings, an old servant does heavy cleaning work and scrubs once or twice a week, and there are those two small tea servers – one for the evening shift, one for the night shift. But those two tea servers have been there for a very long time, they arrange the hours that suit them. Charlie Natto, like Cindy, started at a very young age, but has grown up there. The other tea server, is really not a child, but an old man, he's been at the hotel since it opened, Cindy is very afraid of him, just like being afraid of the manager.

This tea server's name is George Grlek Mr. His uniform is tattered and dirty, but he wears it with honor, his walking appears as if all of these burdens in the hotel are on his shoulders. He knows how to do everything, where every item is placed, what every old customer likes. He can guess the tastes of new customers who have stayed here for a day before. Fawning to please white people, fierce and tyrannical towards his black colleagues, George is the head manager, second only to old Willis. He has to find a mistake in Cindy's work every day, until he likes the child, because Cindy never answered him back, or shirked work like many black children, as George said. After some time, the old man rarely bothered to check Cindy's spittoon and pay attention to the dust in the corners. However, if a person wants to work at this expatriate hotel, he only lets him be unhappy and obedient.

Besides being the tea server head's right-hand man, George is also the public bootlegger in this building. In fact, when he's off work, he hides his alcohol in the hotel's cellar, and Charlie, the other small tea server, sells it to the people in the rooms above who call for it. They don't do other business in this building, but this business is common. Some white women open these rooms,

They tell their customers to buy, and can get some commission from George.

Cindy has learned many tricks from working at this hotel for a long time. "You're really a mute little devil," Charlie constantly taunts him. "But you've only been a lamp for a while, you'll understand in the future."

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

When Will We See the End of Their Evil and Ugliness? 227

— HY

Recently, I saw a copy of the "Northeast News Bulletin" at a friend's house, truly four captivating words.

Opening it up and looking down, the table of contents had two photos of the same size. The photos were on facing pages, and could be said to show two opposite facts. One was titled "May Our Anti-Japanese Heroes Achieve Their Aims," a group photo of the anti-Japanese generals Wang (Delin), Ma (Zhanshan), Su (Bingwen), and Li (Du) returning home and being welcomed in Berlin. The other was the title of this article, except that the author added a "men" character below the word "they" because there was also an explanation below: "A Quick Overview of the Traitorous Puppets of the Northeast Pseudo-Organization." The people in the photo were Puyi, Zheng Xiaoxu, Yuan Jinkai, Xi Qia, Zhang Jinghui, Zhang Hai Peng, Zang Shiyi... etc. Because there were so many people, adding the "men" character seemed appropriate.

Chinese people have a very bad habit, which is that no matter what happens, the approach taken is either to embrace the principle of "each person sweeps the snow from their own doorstep, and doesn't care about the frost on another's roof," or to quietly wait for things to develop naturally. The great Chinese nation has fallen to its current state because of the spread of this bad habit.

What I want to say here is this: The reason why the Northeast has come to its current state is that we are to blame for sitting idly by, waiting for things to happen, and listening to the mistakes of natural development. Your clothes are stolen by robbers, if you don't want to chase after them yourself, and then blame the lost clothes for being covered in mold, it is not something to say that waiting to see how long the mold can grow. What's more, even if in the future there is a great person (in fact, there is none) who helps you chase back the lost clothes, the mold-filled clothes have already lost their original quality!

Applying this metaphor, we cannot help but disagree with the title of this article! Look at when will they do evil? "See when will they do evil?" If you don't want to clear your shame and recover your lost territory yourself, then these puppets will inevitably continue to do evil in the world. Even if they all unfortunately die of a great plague (this is not necessarily possible), there will still be new puppets taking the stage.

Therefore, we cannot sit and "see how long they show their ugliness," we should raise our banners to recover our lost territory, this is when their group of puppets will be destroyed! The birth of new puppets will naturally be even more impossible.

Estrangement 228

— Simon

Estrangement is like a high wall, lying between people, stretching boundlessly. Estrangement, like a pile of wild vines, is planted firmly in my heart, gradually taking root as time goes by. Therefore, the feeling of estrangement becomes thicker day by day. Because of this, it seems that there is an invisible obstacle standing in front of me, separating all the people and things in front of me far away, and everything feels strangely unfamiliar.

Due to estrangement, a sense of indifference to the world arises at the same time, and even if I don't want to be alone, I can't help but be lonely. Estrangement will separate the closeness and sympathy between people, and replace them with suspicion and misunderstanding, leading to a gradual separation. This result is an irreparable defect. Unless estrangement can be eliminated one day, then this defect can be eliminated, but estrangement will always be planted forever, and will continue to increase due to complicated personnel matters.

My thoughts have been eroded by it, resulting in a deformed state. Originally, I had absolutely no hatred for the outside world, but now I don't know why I hate everything so severely. Especially people, whether they are familiar or unfamiliar people I come into contact with every day.

Often, in some kind of situation, some people talk vigorously, and I am also one of the speakers, and what he says may be something that I need to listen to quietly. However, I never have such thoughts. People say what they want, and I just think about what I want; even if it accidentally involves me, I still can't have any inner reaction, and I still pretend not to hear or see. I always think that what people are talking about is not me sitting there, but another invisible me.

No one knows myself as deeply as I do.

If someone comes to find me alone, my pain at this time is unspeakable. No matter how sincere the other person's expression is, or how intimate their words are, I basically believe that it is all fake, a hypocritical performance of smiling with the mouth but not the heart. What the other person gives me is just an inexplicable aversion, aversion, and more aversion. He is talking and saying excitedly, but I am doing evil in my heart. However, face to face, even if I don't want to listen, I have to put on a face that looks like I'm paying attention. I don't know how many times I've encountered this embarrassing situation. Every time I have such a completely reluctant interaction, the feeling of estrangement becomes thicker. In the end, I almost don't even believe myself anymore.

Everyone seems to be living separately. Everyone's emotions and thoughts are also blocked by the high wall of estrangement. I have also reflected carefully, and this may be my own neurotic suspicion. It is not. A few days ago, I ran into an old classmate on the road whom I hadn't seen for many years and could be said to be very friendly with. I once again deeply felt the rare sense of estrangement. At the time, when I saw him, I couldn't help but shout out, shake his hand enthusiastically, and then ask questions about everything, asking if he had been living comfortably these past few years. I was expressing the greatest intimacy as before. However, unexpectedly, he had changed. He was no longer the person I remembered from a few years ago. I asked him a bunch of questions, but he only replied with a few short sentences, and his face was red, and his expression was very unnatural, as if he had met a stranger for the first time. What's going on? Finally, I invited him to pick a place to eat something so we could talk to our heart's content, but he also seemed embarrassed and declined with polite words, saying that he had something to do. After parting, I walked blankly on the bustling road, feeling like I was walking alone in a desolate wilderness. People are estranged from me just as I am estranged from people. We are all living our days estranged from each other!

On the Ship 229

— Xin

A drifter is so easy to be, coming and going indefinitely. Last night, I was still sleeping uneasily in my old school at the foot of Han Mountain, twisting with endless melancholy; tomorrow, I will hurriedly step across Xiangzi Bridge again, board a car and drive to Shantou. Scraped together some money, bought a ship ticket, and left my hometown.

The ship set sail, my hometown was in my misty mind, as if it had sunk. My mind was absorbed by everything on the ship. My stomach was empty, but this chaotic and unbearable wandering life made it impossible to swallow food happily. The money was insufficient, and time was short, so I didn't even try to buy a side dish. It can be said that I was a little too negligent! I took two bites of rice and put it down. The ship was shaking so much that people who were already dizzy could not hold on any longer. I just lay down and quietly endured for three days and three nights. With great difficulty, the night passed. In the morning, people got up to wash their faces, eat porridge, and drink milk. I勉强 climbed up to take a look, still very dizzy, so it was better to lie down again.

The wind was even stronger, and the shaking of the ship caused a commotion throughout the ship. The luggage would jump on its own. The wind and rain blew straight at the drifter squatting near the toilet by the side of the ship, and everything was wet. I grabbed something tightly, leaned against the ship's wall, and endured the sour and unbearable things that were about to be vomited out, my face was pale and blue. The smell of urine and feces from the toilet was not something I had the leisure to enjoy. Dizzy, painful, lazy, sour, hungry, there was not even a place to lie down. Other than secretly crying out in pain, there was no other way! More painful than anything, a poor drifter on the ship! By the time the ship was almost there, the person already looked like they had been sick for several days. The thin face looked like it was pasted with yellow paper. When the ship entered the Wusongkou, most people packed their luggage, put on neat clothes, and waited happily to disembark, but this drifter scrambled to temporarily spread out the group of seats and lay down. When the ship entered the Huangpu River, the Bund was close at hand, and this was when I straightened out my tattered suit.

"Drifting into this big city!" he murmured lowly.

Drifter 230

— Yafei

In the autumn of the year before last, a strange man in tattered clothes suddenly appeared in our town. No one knew where he came from; however, most people in the town looked at him with surprised and suspicious eyes. After arriving here, he settled down in a dilapidated earth shrine less than half a mile from the town. When he came, he brought no bedding or luggage, only a small package and a bamboo flute, drifting here in a carefree manner. What's even stranger is that since he arrived here, almost a year has passed, but he has neither engaged in any business nor begged for food; and he has never been seen speaking a word to anyone. Even when people saw him, they would only glance at him indifferently; no one had the time to pay attention to him.

Since his arrival, in this small town, at the first glimmer of dawn, or on nights with a clear moon and gentle breeze, whether in spring, summer, autumn, or winter, one would always hear a moving, mournful sound. That melody, so melodious and so sorrowful, made people feel, in the deep of night or before dawn, as if they were hearing apes crying in a deserted valley, or a widow lamenting; filling the surrounding environment with a desolate atmosphere! This is the lament of a heartbroken person, the melody of a drifter's heart! Ah, he too is a pitiful person, lonely and desolate!

I detest this evocative tune, yet I love to listen to it; every time I hear this flute sound, it makes me think of myself, recalling the past, and I can't help but shed hot tears. I deeply feel that his life and mine are equally pitiable! Our fates are equally wretched! Our experiences are equally sorrowful!

One evening, I heard this sound and couldn't sleep; so I put on my clothes, got out of bed, and gently opened the door. At this moment, a round, cool moon hung high in the treetops, casting its faint, gentle light; transforming the natural world into a beautiful silver realm. On the azure sky, many stars twinkled, as if cheering for the moon goddess and wanting to conquer this dark world; the autumn insects in the grass seemed to have felt the sorrow of their impending demise! A gust of cool breeze struck my body, which was only covered by a thin garment, making me feel somewhat cold.

All of these elements combined to create a sorrowful world through that mournful melody. But I still followed the sound; walking into a cypress forest, towards a long tomb path. The sound grew closer, and I guessed that it must be coming from here. At this moment, I felt the air was frighteningly eerie; but I finally mustered up my courage and walked forward, and forward. Sure enough, on a small wooden bridge in front of the tomb, sat a person, holding a bamboo flute to his lips and playing.

However, as I approached the small wooden bridge, the flute sound suddenly stopped, and looking again at the bridge, the person was nowhere to be seen; I couldn't help but feel disappointed! Standing on the bridge, I looked around, but there was not a single figure. At this moment, I felt as if I had lost something important, and felt an immeasurable loneliness, emptiness, and sorrow before my eyes!

From that day on, this town, this tomb, this earth shrine, lost that drifter in tattered clothes. Never again, at the first glimmer of dawn, or on nights with a clear moon and gentle breeze, would one hear that moving melody.

"What is going on?" I have always been wondering...

The Sadness of a Clown 231

— Rong

I remember when I was a child in a northern ancient city, walking past a piece of wasteland in front of my old residence at dusk, I often saw many people surrounding a person who resembled a clown, appreciating his "folk art." That person would bow his hands, making many funny gestures, thereby winning the audience's praise and having some copper coins thrown over. When the people gradually dispersed, leaving only him slowly returning home, I noticed the fatigue revealed between his eyebrows. That staggering and desolate scene was even more moving than the tricks he had just performed. At that time, I was still young and didn't quite understand the sorrows of life, but that experience, containing both comedic and tragic elements, constantly stimulated my weak heart, longing for an answer.

In recent days, walking around Stealing Chicken Bridge on Zhejiang Road, I often see people dressed as clowns standing at the entrances of several small shops, some even with painted faces, shouting in strange voices, hoping that people will come into the store to buy things. When I see such a strange image, I am tempted to stop. I and some other people who have stopped for the same reason crowd in front of the clown. The monster wearing a pointed hat and floral clothes then begins to speak, gesticulating wildly amid people's astonished exclamations. Of course, the scene is very comical. However, perhaps because it is overly comical, those who have already squeezed to the door all focus their attention on appreciating the clown, forgetting to go in and buy things. The hand-waving and posing become futile efforts. As a result, people disperse in a burst of laughter. To be honest, even though it is late autumn, some beads of sweat can still be vaguely seen on that clown's face.

I want to laugh, but those beads of sweat make me silent.

We live in the world, and there are many jokes around us. These jokes often stimulate us with novelty, making us laugh involuntarily. However, in the midst of the laughter, few people suddenly fall silent, lifting the outer curtain of joy to see the underlying essence of sadness. When we first see the clown, we should laugh two or three times, but after laughing, if we think about it seriously, we will find that

Page 22

how much desolation this clamor contains, how much bitterness this buffoonery contains. The so-called clowns who amuse people are actually all caused by the ruthless lash of life. In the heart of the former clown, one wonders what is being pondered: an old mother and weak children waiting for food at home. In the heart of the latter clown, one wonders how anxiously he is hoping to preserve a glimmer of hope for his small business, which is in a critical condition, from this economic decline and sluggish market. This is just like a sugar-coated pill, with a delicious sweetness hiding a bitter medicine inside. People often forget the bitterness inside because of the sweetness of the outer taste.

In fact, what we see is so limited. All those prostitutes who force a smile in the dust, those petty officials who ingratiate themselves everywhere, those dancers who deliver flirtatious glances to people while enduring fatigue—aren't they all pitiful creatures who are tossed about by the heavy pressure of life, not even daring to moan?

Mr. Tang Yifang's Work 232

A Gray Story 233

— Sun Yucai

Another year easily passes with the autumn wind. After spending several years in the simple and difficult life of a primary school principal, I stepped into Shanghai's highest educational institution—the Municipal Education Bureau—and began working in social education. In the midst of complex work, I was fortunate enough to recognize some of the meanings of life and the sufferings of society.

This is a gray story, mixed with many tragic overtones.

The fact is this: The bureau director received a letter from the mayor, saying that there was an unemployed youth who had dropped out of school, in a situation of utter desperation, hoping that the mayor would help him. And this task happened to fall on me.

First, I read the youth's letter to the mayor in detail. Although the writing was so immature, his surname was Huang, and he grew up in Zigong City, Sichuan. His family was not bad, so he was able to study at Rong County Literary Academy for two years. Eventually, due to the devastation of bandits and soldiers, and the rampant extortion of civil and military officials, the lives of his family members were reduced to the point where they could not be sustained. He yearned for the prosperity of Shanghai, thinking that Shanghai could indeed give him a way out, so he began his journey. He came to this Paris of the East, but the Paris of the East, while prosperous on one hand, was also starving on the other. He began to feel disappointed, and he felt the danger of the future even more. He was already being invaded by hunger. In this vast journey! He issued a pitiful cry for help to the mayor.

He lives in Central Apartments, a small, dark room. When I rushed in, he was writing a letter, requesting assistance from people in society. He was already ill. I explained my purpose, and he immediately showed a frightened look. He did not expect that a letter would move the mayor's benevolence, sending someone to investigate thoroughly. He told me about his situation as written in the letter, and he described the situation in his hometown of Sichuan in great detail. Then I said to him, "Shanghai can't do anything either. You should go back. You have a family, you have parents, going back is much better than being in Shanghai, right?" He said sadly, "Going back is also a dead end! In today's Zigong City, there is no second way to live except to become a soldier or a bandit. What is the point of going back? Moreover, how can I go back on such a long journey?" Then, he turned out a letter from his father to him. He said, "My parents are also starving!" I read the letter in detail. The general idea was, "In this life surrounded by enemies on all sides, with insufficient food and clothing, I feel the meaninglessness of life. The family can no longer stay together. I don't know if you have found support outside?" I felt even more pressure, and I could no longer sit down. After comforting him with a few words, I ran out of Central Apartments.

A Melancholy Heart 234

— Niqi

To place a melancholy heart on a spring chair, closing my eyes to enjoy these two hours of comfort, this is a strange pastime, and I have been using hairdressing as an excuse for quite some time.

Autumn, a gray season, I walked on Avenue Joffre with a melancholy heart. With both hands in my pants pockets, I leisurely examined the beautiful window display of a store, and then I entered the hair salon with the sign "Electric Perm 3 Yuan".

The spring chair drove away that melancholy heart.

"Shave?" the person in white uniform asked me.

"Haircut." I replied. Turning my head to look in the mirror, I smiled; counting on my fingers, it hasn't even been ten days.

The barber began to work doubtfully.

"A comfortable pastime!" I thought.

Autumn days are short, and all the surrounding electric lights were on. When I put on my autumn coat with both hands, the woman in the mirror smiled and greeted me.

"The owner of that melancholy heart!" My returning heart whispered lowly.

The waiter bowed, opened the door, and the autumn wind was like an arrow, piercing my melancholy heart. I turned up my collar, watching the tips of my own shoes, and walked forward.

Passing by each beautiful window display, I heard a slight voice in my ear:

"Why don't you pay attention to me? I greeted you twice just now!" The owner of the melancholy heart!

"I'm sorry, I didn't hear you," I shook my head, "I didn't think about getting a haircut today."

"This is an unexpected gain, right!"

"We seem to have said that before."

"Please forgive me, I went to another city with him, and I haven't been back for a month. Did you receive my letter?"

"I know. I didn't need you to apologize to me!"

Passing by each beautiful window display, I arrived home.

"Goodbye, I hope for the next "unexpected gain"!"

"You moved, when?"

"The day after I separated from you last year."

"Then you didn't receive my letter?"

"I received them all, thank you. Let's say goodbye." I turned around to take out the key to open the door.

"You are too cruel!" She almost cried.

I wanted to accept this unexpected gain, but my heart told me that she is the owner of melancholy, and you will never be able to sit in the spring chair and enjoy two hours of leisure again.

The door blocked the autumn wind outside, and I collapsed weakly onto the bed, with my melancholy heart.
